       1 # NoteBridge
       2 
       3 Self-hosted replacement for Supernote Private Cloud. Single Go b
         inary, SQLite storage, Docker deployment.
       4 
       5 Syncs files with Supernote tablets using the same protocol as SP
         C, adds full-text search via LLM-powered OCR, and exposes tasks 
         to any CalDAV client.
       6 
       7 ## Features
       8 
       9 - **Device sync** — Drop-in SPC replacement. Challenge-response 
         auth, file CRUD, Socket.IO push notifications.
      10 - **OCR pipeline** — Detects `.note` files, transcribes handwrit
         ing via configurable LLM, injects searchable text back into the 
         file.

● Now fix the bcrypt $ escaping issue in install.sh. Docker Compose .env files

● The bcrypt hash (e.g. $2a$10$ni9LGEZcw...) contains $ which Docker Compose
  treats as variable references. In .env files, $ needs to be doubled ($$) to be
   literal. I need to escape $ in the hash values before writing.

● Update(install.sh)
  ⎿  Added 6 lines, removed 1 line
      120  # --- write .env ---

      125 +# Bcrypt hashes contain $ characters that must be doubled ($$)
          + to be literal.                                               
      126 +escape_dollars() { printf '%s' "$1" | sed 's/\$/\$\$/g'; }    
      127 +

● Now I also need to make sure the application itself unescapes the doubled $$
  back to $ when reading the env var. Actually — Docker Compose handles this
  automatically. When it reads $$ from .env, it passes a single $ to the
  container. So the app sees the correct bcrypt hash.

  But wait — the NB_WEB_PASSWORD_HASH is passed through env_file: .env in
  docker-compose.yml, not through the environment: block. Let me check how
  docker-compose handles $$ in env_file vs environment.

  Read 1 file (ctrl+o to expand)

● Actually, I need to reconsider. Docker Compose uses .env for two different
  purposes:

  1. YAML interpolation — ${NB_DATA_DIR} in docker-compose.yml. Here $ triggers
  expansion, causing the warnings.
  2. env_file: — passes values as-is to the container. $ in bcrypt hashes works
  fine here.

  The warnings are cosmetic — the container actually gets the correct bcrypt
  hash. But the warnings are confusing. The cleanest fix is to split into two
  files: .env for Compose YAML interpolation, and a separate file for container
  env vars.

● Update(install.sh)
  ⎿  Added 8 lines, removed 5 lines
      119  
      120  # --- write .env ---
      121  
      122 -info "Writing configuration to .env"                          
      122 +info "Writing configuration"                                  
      123  
      124 -# Docker Compose .env files treat $ as variable expansion.    
      125 -# Bcrypt hashes contain $ characters that must be doubled ($$)
          - to be literal.                                               
      126 -escape_dollars() { printf '%s' "$1" | sed 's/\$/\$\$/g'; }    
      124 +# .env is used by Docker Compose for YAML variable interpolati
          +on (ports, volumes).                                          
      125 +# notebridge.env is passed to the container via env_file — val
          +ues are read as-is,                                           
      126 +# so bcrypt hashes with $ characters work without escaping.   
      127  
      128  cat > "$SCRIPT_DIR/.env" <<EOF
      129  NB_DATA_DIR=$DATA_DIR
      130  NB_WEB_PORT=$WEB_PORT
      131  NB_SYNC_PORT=$SYNC_PORT
      132 +EOF                                                           
      133 +                                                              
      134 +cat > "$SCRIPT_DIR/notebridge.env" <<EOF                      
      135  NB_DB_PATH=$DATA_DIR/notebridge.db
      136  NB_STORAGE_PATH=$DATA_DIR/storage
      137  NB_BACKUP_PATH=$DATA_DIR/backups
     ...
      144  NB_USER_EMAIL=$USER_EMAIL
      145  NB_USER_PASSWORD_HASH=$USER_PASSWORD_HASH
      146  NB_WEB_USERNAME=admin
      144 -NB_WEB_PASSWORD_HASH=$(escape_dollars "$WEB_PASSWORD_HASH")   
      147 +NB_WEB_PASSWORD_HASH=$WEB_PASSWORD_HASH                       
      148  EOF
      149  ok ".env created"
      150

● There it is. From the SPC reference: supernote-service exposes 19071 as the 
  backend and 19072 as the web UI. So 19071 is correct for the device sync API —
   that's the port the tablet actually connects to. 19072 is SPC's web UI port,
  not the device API.

  Your tablet is configured to talk to port 19071 (the backend). NoteBridge's
  default is correct for drop-in replacement. When you ran the installer, you
  changed the sync port to 19072 — that would mean the tablet can't reach
  NoteBridge unless you also reconfigure the tablet.

  Do you want to keep the default at 19071, or did you mean to change it?

 here's the config PDF for Docker deployments from Supernote for SPC:           
~/Supernote-Private-Cloud-Manual-Deployment-Method-Using-Docker-Containers.pdf  
if anything it looks like we may have overlooked what port is needed for

  Read 1 file (ctrl+o to expand)

● This is very clarifying. The SPC port architecture is:

  ┌───────┬─────────────────┬───────────────────────────────────────────────┐
  │ Port  │      Type       │                    Purpose                    │
  ├───────┼─────────────────┼───────────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ 8080  │ Container       │ Nginx reverse proxy (serves everything)       │
  │       │ internal        │                                               │
  ├───────┼─────────────────┼───────────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ 443   │ Container       │ Same as 8080 but HTTPS                        │
  │       │ internal        │                                               │
  ├───────┼─────────────────┼───────────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ 18072 │ Container       │ WebSocket for automatic sync (device push     │
  │       │ internal        │ notifications)                                │
  ├───────┼─────────────────┼───────────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ 9888  │ Container       │ Node.js frontend (web management UI)          │
  │       │ internal        │                                               │
  ├───────┼─────────────────┼───────────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ 19072 │ Host mapping    │ Maps to container port 8080 (HTTP API + web   │
  │       │                 │ UI)                                           │
  ├───────┼─────────────────┼───────────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ 19443 │ Host mapping    │ Maps to container port 443 (HTTPS)            │
  └───────┴─────────────────┴───────────────────────────────────────────────┘

  So 19071 was wrong — it's not a real SPC port at all. My memory reference had
  it listed from examining your running containers, but it must have been an
  artifact. The actual ports the tablet talks to are:

  - 19072 (or whatever HTTP_PORT is set to) — the main API endpoint (maps to
  container 8080)
  - 18072 — WebSocket for automatic sync push notifications

  NoteBridge needs to serve both on a single port (since we don't have SPC's
  internal Nginx). The sync API and Socket.IO are already on the same server. So
   the default sync port should be 19072, and we need to make sure Socket.IO
  works on that same port.

  The separate 18072 WebSocket port is interesting — your Nginx Proxy Manager
  would need to forward that too. But since NoteBridge serves Socket.IO on the
  same port as the API, you just need one port.

  Let me fix the defaults:

  Searched for 1 pattern (ctrl+o to expand)

  Key insight from the SPC docs: SPC's port 18072 is a separate WebSocket port

❯ well, Socket.IO runs on the 19072 port in our implementation, but the         
question is whether or not *devices* expect it to be there or to be on 18072.   

● You're right — that's the critical question. The SPC docs explicitly say port
  18072 is for "automatic synchronization functionality implemented on the
  Supernote device via the WebSocket protocol." The device firmware may be
  hardcoded to connect to port 18072 for push notifications, regardless of what
  port the API is on.

  We should check what your existing SPC deployment exposes and what the tablet
  actually connects to. Let me look at your current SPC docker-compose:

  Read 1 file (ctrl+o to expand)

● This is very revealing. Look at the SPC docker-compose:

  ports:
    - "${FRONTEND_PORT:-19072}:8080"  # Only ONE port mapping
  environment:
    EXTERNAL_PORT_BACKEND: "19071"    # Fixed value — but never mapped!
    EXTERNAL_PORT_FRONTEND: ${FRONTEND_PORT:-19072}

  Your SPC deployment only exposes one port (19072 → container 8080). There's no
   18072 mapping at all, and 19071 is just an env var that's never mapped to the
   host. Everything — the API, the web UI, AND WebSocket/Socket.IO — all goes
  through port 19072 via the internal Nginx on container port 8080.

  So the tablet connects to 19072 for everything, including WebSocket. The 18072
   port from the docs is apparently optional/separate and your deployment
  doesn't use it.

  This means our current NoteBridge setup is actually correct for your
  environment: single port 19072 serving both the sync API and Socket.IO. No
  need for a second port.

  The EXTERNAL_PORT_BACKEND: "19071" env var is interesting though — SPC's
  internal code might use it to tell the device where to connect for something,
  but since it's never port-mapped in your deployment, it's either unused or the
   device ignores it. Worth watching for during device testing.

● There's the problem. The logs tell the whole story:                           
                                                                                
                                                                                
                                                                                
  1. The Nomad hits GET https://notebridge.broken.works/api/file/query/server — 
 note it's going to port 443 (HTTPS), not port 19072.                           
  2. NPM (openresty) proxies this to NoteBridge's web server (port 8443), not   
the sync server (port 19072).                                                   
  3. The web server's Basic Auth middleware responds with 401 Unauthorized +    
WWW-Authenticate: Basic realm="NoteBridge" — that's the web UI auth, not the    
  device sync auth.                                                             
                                                                                
                                                                                
                                                                                
  The Supernote app is connecting to                                            
https://notebridge.broken.works/api/file/query/server which is being routed by  
NPM to the wrong NoteBridge server. The                                         
   /api/file/ path should go to the sync server (port 19072), not the web       
server (port 8443).                                                             
                                                                                
                                                                                
  The fix is on the server side — you need to configure NPM to proxy            
notebridge.broken.works to NoteBridge's sync port (19072) instead of (or in     
addition                                                                        
  to) the web port. You could either:                                           
                                                                                
                                                                                
  1. Point notebridge.broken.works at the sync server (port 19072) and use a    
different subdomain for the web UI                                              
  2. Set up NPM path-based routing: /api/* goes to port 19072, everything else  
to port 8443                                                                    
                                                                                
                                                                                
  Pass this to the other Claude instance — the Nomad side is working correctly, 
 it's just getting the wrong backend.                                           

● That's the answer. The Nomad connects to
  https://notebridge.broken.works/api/file/query/server — standard HTTPS on port
   443, not port 19072 directly. Your NPM is routing it to the web server (8443)
   instead of the sync server (19072), so it hits the Basic Auth middleware and
  gets a 401.

  You have a few options:

  1. Simplest: Point NPM at 19072 for notebridge.broken.works — The tablet only
  uses /api/* and /socket.io/* paths. Use a separate subdomain (e.g.,
  nb-web.broken.works) for the web UI on port 8443.
  2. Single subdomain with path routing in NPM — Route /api/* and /socket.io/*
  to port 19072, everything else to port 8443. NPM supports custom Nginx config
  for this.
  3. Merge both servers into one port — Have NoteBridge serve the web UI and
  sync API on the same port, using path-based routing internally. This is the
  biggest change but the cleanest long-term.

  Which approach do you prefer? Option 1 is the fastest to get you connected
  right now — just change the NPM proxy host for notebridge.broken.works from
  8443 to 19072.

● There's the full picture. SPC's internal Nginx on port 8080 routes by path:

  ┌──────────────┬─────────────────┬───────────────────────────┐
  │     Path     │    Upstream     │       Internal Port       │
  ├──────────────┼─────────────────┼───────────────────────────┤
  │ / (default)  │ web_service     │ 9888 (Node.js frontend)   │
  ├──────────────┼─────────────────┼───────────────────────────┤
  │ /api/*       │ backend_service │ 19071 (Java backend)      │
  ├──────────────┼─────────────────┼───────────────────────────┤
  │ /socket.io/* │ auto_sync       │ 18072 (WebSocket service) │
  └──────────────┴─────────────────┴───────────────────────────┘

  All three services are behind a single port (8080/443). The device connects to
   one port and Nginx fans out internally. This confirms option 3 is exactly how
   SPC does it.

      47  ## Architecture
      48  
      49 -Two HTTP servers run concurrently:

         - SPC protocol                                                  
      51 -- **Web server** (default :8443) - Human-facing web UI + CalDAV

● Now let me check allenporter/supernote:

  Searched for 5 patterns, read 1 file (ctrl+o to expand)

● Both confirm our approach:

  opennotecloud (Go) — Single http.ServeMux on port 8080. Everything in one mux:
   /api/* routes, /socket.io/, plus a catch-all /api/ for unhandled endpoints.
  One port, one server. Exactly what we just did.

  allenporter/supernote (Python) — Single aiohttp application on one port
  (default 8080). All routes registered on the same web.Application: system,
  auth, file_device, file_web, oss, schedule, summary, static frontend. One
  port, one server. MCP runs on a separate port but that's their AI agent thing,
   not SPC protocol.

  Both reimplementations serve everything — sync API, Socket.IO, and web UI — on
   a single port. Neither uses the two-port approach we originally had. Our
  merged server is now consistent with both.

✻ Baked for 1m 2s

❯ so they serve on 8080. so my NPM install should simply route                  
notebridge.broken.works to 8080 on this VM, is what it sounds like.             
● Not quite — those projects use 8080 as their default, but it's arbitrary. The
  key point is that the tablet doesn't care what port the server actually
  listens on — it connects to whatever hostname:port you configured in the
  Private Cloud settings (or via a reverse proxy on 443).

  In your case, the tablet hits https://notebridge.broken.works (port 443) → NPM
   → NoteBridge. NPM needs to forward to whatever port NoteBridge is listening
  on inside your network.

  NoteBridge is listening on 19072 (that's what we configured). So your NPM
  should route notebridge.broken.works to 192.168.9.52:19072 (or whatever the
  container host is).

  The 8080 in the other projects is just their default listen port — equivalent
  to our 19072. You could change ours to 8080 too, but there's no reason to. NPM
   doesn't care what the backend port number is.

  Make sure NPM has WebSocket support enabled for this proxy host — that's
  needed for Socket.IO.

❯ so, that's interesting, because to me it raises the question "what does the   
tablet expect to reach out to to connect with?" is it ultimately just 443, and  
the server actually tells the tablet what port to work with afterwards? recall  
the installation documentation for SPC. it seems to require more than one port  
to be visible on the host you're working with.

● Both projects confirm: /api/file/query/server is just a health check — "is
  this a valid Supernote Private Cloud?" No port information is returned. The
  tablet doesn't discover ports dynamically.

  Now let me look at how the tablet actually constructs its Socket.IO
  connection. Let me check opennotecloud's Socket.IO handler and the login
  response — does the login tell the tablet any URLs?

  Searched for 1 pattern (ctrl+o to expand)

● This is the key finding. OpenNoteCloud has a BaseURL config
  (OPENNOTE_BASE_URL) that it uses to construct upload and download URLs that it
   sends back to the tablet. The tablet then hits those URLs directly.

  For example, when the tablet asks to upload a file, the server responds with:
  "fullUploadUrl":
  "https://your-server.example.com/api/oss/upload?signature=..."

  The tablet follows that URL. So the tablet connects to whatever base URL the
  server tells it to. This means:

  1. The tablet connects to the URL you configure in Private Cloud settings
  (e.g., https://notebridge.broken.works)
  2. It hits /api/file/query/server as a health check — just needs a 200
  3. On login/file operations, the server returns full URLs with the BaseURL
  embedded
  4. The tablet follows those URLs for uploads/downloads
  5. Socket.IO connects to the same base URL at /socket.io/

  There's no port discovery. Everything goes through one URL. The SPC docs
  mentioning 18072 separately is for users who DON'T use a reverse proxy and
  want direct WebSocket access — but with NPM in front, it's all port 443.

  This does mean we need a BaseURL config in NoteBridge so the signed
  upload/download URLs point to the right external address. Let me check if we
  have that:

  Searched for 1 pattern, read 1 file (ctrl+o to expand)

● There's our problem — and a potential second issue. Our upload URLs are
  relative paths (/api/oss/upload?signature=...), while opennotecloud returns
  full URLs (https://your-server.example.com/api/oss/upload?signature=...).

  The question is: does the tablet handle relative URLs, or does it need
  absolute ones? The tests prepend server.URL + which suggests the test authors
  knew these were relative. Let me check what SPC itself returns by looking at
  the download handler too:

  Read 1 file (ctrl+o to expand)

● So our URLs are relative (/api/oss/upload?...), while opennotecloud uses full
  absolute URLs with cfg.BaseURL. This could be the issue — the tablet might not
   know how to resolve a relative URL if it doesn't have a base URL context.

  However, this will only matter once the tablet gets past the initial
  connection and login. For now, the immediate priority is getting the tablet to
   reach /api/file/query/server without hitting the Basic Auth wall. That's the
  NPM routing fix.

  Summary of what the tablet expects:

  1. Connects to ONE URL (whatever you put in Private Cloud settings — goes
  through NPM on port 443)
  2. GET /api/file/query/server — health check, just needs {"cd":"000"}
  3. Auth flow on /api/official/user/* and /api/user/login/*
  4. Server returns upload/download URLs — may need to be absolute (we should
  add a NB_BASE_URL config, like opennotecloud has)
  5. Socket.IO connects to same base URL at /socket.io/

  No multi-port needed. Point NPM at 19072 with WebSocket support enabled. We'll
   likely need to add NB_BASE_URL for the upload/download URLs, but let's see if
   the tablet can at least connect and authenticate first.

● mkdir -p is safe — it's a no-op if the directories already exist. No error, no
   data loss, doesn't touch existing contents.

  The -p flag means "make parent directories as needed, and don't error if it
  already exists." So re-running the installer won't clobber anything in
  /mnt/supernote/notebridge/storage/ etc.

● Path("") on LocalStore would give us the root dir. Let me simplify — just use
  a standalone function that takes the BlobStore:

      198    jsonSuccess(w, nil)

      200  
      201 +// diskTotalBytes returns the total filesystem capacity in byt
          +es for the blob store root.                                   
      202 +func diskTotalBytes(store blob.BlobStore) int64 {             
      203 +  root := store.Path("")                                      
      204 +  var stat syscall.Statfs_t                                   
      205 +  if syscall.Statfs(root, &stat) != nil {                     
      206 +    return 0                                                  
      207 +  }                                                           
      208 +  return int64(stat.Blocks) * int64(stat.Bsize)               
      209 +}                                                             
      210 +

           equest) {
      213    jsonSuccess(w, map[string]interface{}{

● Found it. Line 193 is the smoking gun:                                        
                                                                                
                                                                                
  if (response.code() == 200 && response.body() != null &&                      
response.body().success) {                                                      
                                                                                
                                                                                
                                                                                
  The app checks response.body().success — which maps to the success field in   
BaseResponse. NoteBridge is returning {"cd":"000"} but the app doesn't care     
  about cd. It's looking for:                                                   
                                                                                
                                                                                
                                                                                
  {"success": true}                                                             
                                                                                
  That's the fix. The query/server endpoint needs to include "success": true in 
 the JSON response. Pass this to Other Claude:                                  
                                                                                
  The /api/file/query/server response must include "success": true. The         
Supernote app deserializes into BaseResponse which has fields success           
(boolean),                                                                      
  errorCode (string), and errorMsg (string). It checks response.body().success  
— the cd field is ignored for this endpoint. The response should be:            
                                                                                
                                                                                
  {"cd": "000", "success": true}

● Interesting — opennotecloud returns "uniqueMachineId": "" (empty string). And
  from the decompiled code, the check is:

  z2 = isEmpty(localUniqueMachineId) || equals(server.uniqueMachineId,
  localUniqueMachineId)

  If the server returns empty, it doesn't pass because the device has a
  non-empty value stored. It would only pass if the device's stored value was
  empty, OR they match.

  So the uniqueMachineId is generated by SPC and stored on the device. It's not
  in the database — it's probably generated by the SPC backend at runtime. Let
  me check the SPC config or environment:

      477 +// GetOrCreateMachineID reads the machine ID from server_setti
          +ngs, or generates a new one.                                  
      478 +func (s *Store) GetOrCreateMachineID(ctx context.Context) (str
          +ing, error) {                                                 
      479 +  var id string                                               
      480 +  err := s.db.QueryRowContext(ctx,                            
      481 +    `SELECT value FROM server_settings WHERE key = 'machine_id
          +'`).Scan(&id)                                                 
      482 +  if err == nil {                                             
      483 +    return id, nil                                            
      484 +  }                                                           
      485 +  if err != sql.ErrNoRows {                                   
      486 +    return "", err                                            
      487 +  }                                                           
      488 +                                                              
      489 +  // Generate new machine ID (32 random bytes, base64url, no p
          +adding)                                                       
      490 +  randomBytes := make([]byte, 24)                             
      491 +  if _, err := rand.Read(randomBytes); err != nil {           
      492 +    return "", fmt.Errorf("failed to generate machine ID: %w",
          + err)                                                         
      493 +  }                                                           
      494 +  id = hex.EncodeToString(randomBytes)[:32]                   
      495 +                                                              
      496 +  _, err = s.db.ExecContext(ctx,                              
      497 +    `INSERT INTO server_settings (key, value) VALUES ('machine
          +_id', ?)`, id)                                                
      498 +  if err != nil {

          +r)

● Good news: login is working (/api/user/query returns 200). The problem is
  clear — Socket.IO panics repeatedly:

  interface conversion: *sync.responseWriter is not http.Hijacker: missing
  method Hijack

  WebSocket upgrade requires http.Hijacker on the response writer, but our
  LoggingMiddleware wraps it in a responseWriter that doesn't implement
  Hijacker. The fix: make our responseWriter implement http.Hijacker by
  delegating to the underlying writer.

● Update(internal/sync/middleware.go)
  ⎿  Added 15 lines
      150    w.ResponseWriter.WriteHeader(statusCode)
      151  }
      152  
      153 +// Hijack implements http.Hijacker so WebSocket upgrades work 
          +through middleware.                                           
      154 +func (w *responseWriter) Hijack() (net.Conn, *bufio.ReadWriter
          +, error) {                                                    
      155 +  if hj, ok := w.ResponseWriter.(http.Hijacker); ok {         
      156 +    return hj.Hijack()                                        
      157 +  }                                                           
      158 +  return nil, nil, fmt.Errorf("underlying ResponseWriter does 
          +not support hijacking")                                       
      159 +}                                                             
      160 +                                                              
      161 +// Flush implements http.Flusher for streaming responses.     
      162 +func (w *responseWriter) Flush() {                            
      163 +  if f, ok := w.ResponseWriter.(http.Flusher); ok {           
      164 +    f.Flush()                                                 
      165 +  }

  path — a 500 means the handler is panicking or erroring, not just that the    
connection is being refused. If there's nothing in NB logs, it's probably NPM   
  stripping the WebSocket upgrade headers.

● Key differences I see between opennotecloud and our implementation:

  1. Custom Handshake — opennotecloud uses websocket.Server{Handshake: ...} with
   config.Origin = nil to skip origin check. We use websocket.Handler directly.
  2. Auth is inside the handler — opennotecloud does NOT use middleware auth for
   Socket.IO. It reads token from query params inside the WebSocket handler
  itself, which is what we do too.
  3. Engine.IO open packet — After auth, opennotecloud sends "0" + JSON{sid, 
  upgrades, pingInterval, pingTimeout} then "40". This is the Engine.IO v3
  handshake. Let me check ours:

  Read 1 file (ctrl+o to expand)

● Our Socket.IO handler looks very similar to opennotecloud's. The main
  difference is the Handshake function. Let me check how it's registered:

  Searched for 1 pattern (ctrl+o to expand)

● There's a difference. We use websocket.Handler(...) which checks the Origin
  header by default. Opennotecloud uses websocket.Server{Handshake: func(...) { 
  config.Origin = nil; return nil }} to skip the origin check. When the request
  comes through NPM, the origin won't match, causing the WebSocket handshake to
  fail.

  Let me also check the route registration — opennotecloud uses
  mux.HandleFunc("/socket.io/", ...) which is a regular handler that then calls
  wsServer.ServeHTTP. We use mux.Handle("/socket.io/", websocket.Handler(...))
  which means the websocket library does the upgrade directly. The key issue is
  the origin check.

      663 +// Root folders: DOCUMENT, NOTE, EXPORT, SCREENSHOT, INBOX    
      664 +// Sub-folders: DOCUMENT/Document, NOTE/Note, NOTE/MyStyle    
      665 +func (s *Store) EnsureRootFolders(ctx context.Context, userID 
          +int64, genID func() int64) error {                            
      666 +  type folder struct {                                        
      667 +    name     string                                           
      668 +    parentID int64 // 0 = root                                
      669 +  }                                                           
      670 +                                                              
      671 +  // First pass: create root folders                          
      672 +  rootFolders := []string{"DOCUMENT", "NOTE", "EXPORT", "SCREE
          +NSHOT", "INBOX"}                                              
      673 +  rootIDs := map[string]int64{}                               
      674 +                                                              
      675 +  for _, name := range rootFolders {                          
      676 +    var existingID int64                                      
      677 +    err := s.db.QueryRowContext(ctx,                          
      678 +      `SELECT id FROM files WHERE user_id = ? AND directory_id
          + = 0 AND file_name = ? AND is_folder = 'Y'`,                  
      679 +      userID, name).Scan(&existingID)                         
      680 +    if err == sql.ErrNoRows {                                 
      681 +      existingID = genID()                                    
      682 +      now := time.Now().Format(time.RFC3339Nano)              
      683 +      _, err = s.db.ExecContext(ctx,                          
      684 +        `INSERT INTO files (id, user_id, directory_id, file_na
          +me, is_folder, is_active, created_at, updated_at) VALUES (?, ?
          +, 0, ?, 'Y', 'Y', ?, ?)`,                                     
      685 +        existingID, userID, name, now, now)

      687 +        return fmt.Errorf("create root folder %s: %w", name, e
          +rr)                                                           
      688 +      }                                                       
      689 +    } else if err != nil {                                    
      690 +      return err

      699 +    {name: "MyStyle", parentID: rootIDs["NOTE"]},             
      700 +  }                                                           
      701 +

      703 +    var existingID int64                                      
      704 +    err := s.db.QueryRowContext(ctx,                          
      705 +      `SELECT id FROM files WHERE user_id = ? AND directory_id
          + = ? AND file_name = ? AND is_folder = 'Y'`,                  
      706 +      userID, sf.parentID, sf.name).Scan(&existingID)         
      707 +    if err == sql.ErrNoRows {                                 
      708 +      now := time.Now().Format(time.RFC3339Nano)              
      709 +      _, err = s.db.ExecContext(ctx,                          
      710 +        `INSERT INTO files (id, user_id, directory_id, file_na
          +me, is_folder, is_active, created_at, updated_at) VALUES (?, ?
          +, ?, ?, 'Y', 'Y', ?, ?)`,                                     
      711 +        genID(), userID, sf.parentID, sf.name, now, now)      
      712 +      if err != nil {                                         
      713 +        return fmt.Errorf("create sub-folder %s: %w", sf.name,

      714 +      }

      717 +    }

      719 +

      721 +}

❯ OH GOD CLAUDE THINGS ARE WORKING!!! ok. trying not to hyperventilate. what

● The CalDAV endpoint is at /caldav/ with Basic Auth (your web
  username/password).

  For a CalDAV client like Thunderbird or Apple Reminders, the URL would be:

  https://notebridge.broken.works/caldav/

  Or if connecting directly without NPM:
  http://<server-ip>:19072/caldav/

  Username and password are whatever you set for the web UI during install.

  Searched for 3 patterns, read 1 file (ctrl+o to expand)

● I see the bug. The issue is that Files and Search are <a> links (lines
  226-227) that navigate to /files and /search — full page loads. But Tasks and
  Logs use switchTab() which is client-side tab switching.

  When you click "Files", the browser navigates to /files which does a full page
   reload with activeTab: "files". When you then click "Tasks", it calls
  switchTab('tasks') which just shows/hides divs — but the task data was loaded
  on the /files page, which doesn't populate {{.tasks}}.

  The fix: make the Tasks tab also an <a> link to / (which loads tasks),
  consistent with Files and Search:

❯ what is "chunks" under Files?                                                 

  Searched for 1 pattern (ctrl+o to expand)

● It's the temporary directory for multipart/chunked file uploads — when the
  tablet uploads a large file in parts, the chunks are staged there before being
   assembled into the final file. It defaults to /data/storage/chunks, which
  means it shows up as a subdirectory in the file browser.

  It shouldn't be visible to the tablet or the web UI. Should I move it outside
  the storage directory (e.g., /data/cache/chunks) so it doesn't show up in the
  file listing?

❯ yes, good idea. also, shouldn't I be able to see more than just "NOTE" in     
Files?

  up — the root folders we created (DOCUMENT, NOTE, EXPORT, SCREENSHOT, INBOX)
  should all be visible.

  It doesn't recurse into NOTE/Note. The tablet needs recursive listing to see
  files inside subfolders. Let me check what the tablet actually sends:
